###begin article-title 0
###xml 61 66 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Essential Role of Chromatin Remodeling Protein Bptf in Early Mouse Embryos and Embryonic Stem Cells
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: JL AAS HX MSHK TPY CW. Performed the experiments: JL YP LVS EAS JM. Analyzed the data: JL AAS. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: JL LT YEZ MSHK MRK TPY CW. Wrote the paper: JL AAS MRK TPY CW.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 207 211 207 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 358 361 358 361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 354 361 354 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 509 513 509 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 708 711 708 711 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 704 711 704 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 913 918 913 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf-</italic>
###xml 1324 1329 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
We have characterized the biological functions of the chromatin remodeling protein Bptf (Bromodomain PHD-finger Transcription Factor), the largest subunit of NURF (Nucleosome Remodeling Factor) in a mammal. Bptf mutants manifest growth defects at the post-implantation stage and are reabsorbed by E8.5. Histological analyses of lineage markers show that Bptf-/- embryos implant but fail to establish a functional distal visceral endoderm. Microarray analysis at early stages of differentiation has identified Bptf-dependent gene targets including homeobox transcriptions factors and genes essential for the development of ectoderm, mesoderm, and both definitive and visceral endoderm. Differentiation of Bptf-/- embryonic stem cell lines into embryoid bodies revealed its requirement for development of mesoderm, endoderm, and ectoderm tissue lineages, and uncovered many genes whose activation or repression are Bptf-dependent. We also provide functional and physical links between the Bptf-containing NURF complex and the Smad transcription factors. These results suggest that Bptf may co-regulate some gene targets of this pathway, which is essential for establishment of the visceral endoderm. We conclude that Bptf likely regulates genes and signaling pathways essential for the development of key tissues of the early mouse embryo.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 557 561 557 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 776 780 776 780 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1002 1006 1002 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1156 1160 1156 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1350 1354 1347 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 634 639 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1401 1406 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
While the chromatin of eukaryotes provides an efficient means to compact large amounts of DNA into a small nucleus, it renders the DNA relatively inaccessible. ATP-dependent chromatin remodeling complexes mobilize nucleosomes and provide a means to gain access to DNA in chromatin. While the biochemical functions of chromatin remodeling complexes is well-characterized, less is known of their biological functions. In this manuscript, we elucidate the biological functions of Bptf, a subunit of the NURF chromatin remodeling complex. Our studies show that Bptf is required for the establishment of the anterior-posterior axis of the mouse embryo during the earliest stages of development. To understand its functions in tissue differentiation, we generated and characterized Bptf-mutant ES cells. Mutant embryonic stem cells show significant defects in the differentiation of ectoderm, endoderm, and mesoderm. Genome-wide analysis of gene expression defects during differentiation has identified many Bptf-dependent pathways including key regulators of ectoderm, endoderm, and mesoderm differentiation. Moreover, we have identified critical functions for Bptf during the TGFbeta/Smad-induced expression of visceral endoderm and mesoderm markers, an important signaling pathway in the early embryo. These results suggest that chromatin remodeling by Bptf regulates key signaling pathways in the early mouse embryo.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Introduction
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 404 407 404 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Jin1">[1]</xref>
###xml 408 411 408 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Margueron1">[3]</xref>
###xml 725 728 725 728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Eberharter1">[4]</xref>
###xml 729 732 729 732 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Bao1">[5]</xref>
The packaging of eukaryotic DNA into chromatin provides a general mechanism for the modulation of gene activity and DNA metabolism through alterations of chromatin architecture. The structure and composition of chromatin can be altered by a number of distinct pathways, including post-translational modification of histones, ATP-dependent remodeling of nucleosomes, and incorporation of histone variants [1]-[3]. ATP-dependent chromatin remodeling is catalyzed by the large and conserved SWI/SNF super family of multi-subunit chromatin remodeling enzymes that are classified into four major subfamilies (SWI/SNF, ISWI, CHD, and INO80), and distinguished by the common presence of a SWI2/SNF2-related catalytic ATPase subunit [4],[5].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 114 117 114 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Corona1">[6]</xref>
###xml 118 121 118 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Dirscherl1">[7]</xref>
###xml 294 297 294 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Banting1">[8]</xref>
###xml 298 301 298 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Mizuguchi1">[9]</xref>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tsukiyama1">[10]</xref>
###xml 558 566 558 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 566 569 566 569 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Mizuguchi1">[9]</xref>
###xml 717 724 717 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 777 781 777 781 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Badenhorst1">[11]</xref>
###xml 908 912 908 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Badenhorst1">[11]</xref>
###xml 913 917 913 917 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Badenhorst2">[13]</xref>
###xml 999 1003 999 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Wysocka1">[14]</xref>
###xml 1304 1308 1304 1308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Barak1">[15]</xref>
###xml 1416 1420 1416 1420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Barak1">[15]</xref>
###xml 421 431 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 447 457 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 700 710 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 1005 1010 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
###xml 1056 1066 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 1333 1338 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1393 1403 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
The mammalian ISWI chromatin remodeling complexes contain either one of two related ISWI ATPases, Snf2l and Snf2h [6],[7]. The Snf2l ATPase is contained in two assemblies-NURF (Nucleosome Remodeling Factor), which is dedicated to the regulation of transcription, and the recently reported CERF [8],[9]. NURF is the founding member of the ISWI family of chromatin remodeling complexes, and was originally characterized in Drosophila [10]. Purified Drosophila NURF catalyzes ATP-dependent nucleosome sliding and promotes transcription from chromatin templates in vitro[9]. As shown by whole genome expression studies of mutants, NURF positively or negatively regulates transcription of several hundred Drosophila genes in vivo, including many genes important for fly development [11]. This is likely accomplished through recruitment of NURF301, the largest NURF subunit, by gene-specific transcription factors [11]-[13], and binding of a PHD finger of NURF301 to tri-methylated lysine 4 on histone H3 [14]. Human NURF contains the orthologs of three of four Drosophila NURF components-BPTF (Bromodomain PHD-finger Transcription Factor), the mammalian counterpart of NURF301, SNF2L (the ISWI ATPase) and RbAp46/48, a WD-40 repeat histone-binding protein found in several chromatin-related protein complexes [15]. Biochemical studies of human NURF have shown that it has similar properties to its Drosophila counterpart [15].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 182 209 182 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Brg1, Brm, Chd4, Chd2, p400</italic>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Etl1</italic>
###xml 320 324 320 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Williams1">[16]</xref>
###xml 325 329 325 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Roberts1">[22]</xref>
###xml 500 504 500 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Stopka1">[23]</xref>
###xml 667 670 667 670 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Corona1">[6]</xref>
###xml 671 674 671 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Dirscherl1">[7]</xref>
###xml 129 134 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 370 376 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
The physiological functions of an increasing number of mammalian chromatin remodeling complexes have been revealed by studies of mouse mutants for the catalytic ATPase. Mutations in Brg1, Brm, Chd4, Chd2, p400 and Etl1 have been shown to be required for proper embryonic development, hematopoiesis or postnatal survival [16]-[22]. A mutant for the Snf2h, one of the two murine ISWI ATPases, revealed severe proliferation defects in the early embryo, resulting in a peri-implantation lethal phenotype [23]. Given the presence of Snf2h in multiple chromatin remodeling complexes, the assignment of biological phenotypes to different enzyme complexes can be problematic [6],[7].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 233 240 233 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NURF301</italic>
###xml 281 285 281 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Xiao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 466 470 466 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Badenhorst1">[11]</xref>
###xml 471 475 471 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Badenhorst2">[13]</xref>
###xml 556 560 556 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACF1</italic>
###xml 762 770 762 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Polycomb</italic>
###xml 783 787 783 787 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Fyodorov1">[24]</xref>
###xml 172 182 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 222 232 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 545 555 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
By analysis of mutations of unique subunits it is possible to identify the biological functions of different Snf2h-containing complexes. This has been accomplished for the Drosophila ISWI complexes. Studies of mutants for Drosophila NURF301, which is exclusive to the NURF complex [12], have revealed a late larval-lethal phenotype and mis-expression of homeotic selector genes and genes involved in the response to heat stress, cytokine and steroid hormone signals [11],[13]. These phenotypes do not overlap with those observed for mutants for Drosophila ACF1 (a component of the ISWI-containing complexes ACF and CHRAC) which are impaired in the establishment and/or maintenance of transcriptional silencing in pericentric heterochromatin and in repression by Polycomb-group genes [24].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 123 127 123 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Barak1">[15]</xref>
###xml 155 159 155 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 105 110 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 361 366 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To elucidate the biological roles of Bptf-containing complexes we have generated embryonic stem cell and mouse mutants for Bptf[15]. Our studies show that Bptf mutant phenotypes begin to manifest just after implantation stage, and mutant embryos are completely reabsorbed by embryonic day (E) 8.5. Genetic and molecular analysis in embryonic stem cells and the mouse suggest a role for Bptf in the development of visceral endoderm (VE) of the early mammalian embryo. We propose that Bptf is required for the development of the VE, and more importantly the distal visceral endoderm (DVE), in part through regulating cellular proliferation, the expression of homeobox-containing transcription factors and pathways regulated by the Smad transcription factors, a major conduit for cell signaling in development. These findings suggest a model in which the activities of Bptf-containing complexes, likely the NURF remodeling complex, regulate cell proliferation and embryonic development and therefore are essential in the post-implantation embryo.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
Results/Discussion
###end title 11
###begin title 12
###xml 57 61 57 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Characterization of Gene-Trap and Conditional Alleles of Bptf
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 145 155 145 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s001">Figure S1A</xref>
###xml 157 161 157 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Xiao1">[12]</xref>
###xml 162 166 162 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Barak1">[15]</xref>
###xml 167 171 167 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Jones1">[25]</xref>
###xml 365 387 365 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s001">Figure S1B, Figure S1C</xref>
###xml 518 528 518 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s001">Figure S1D</xref>
###xml 650 660 650 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s001">Figure S1E</xref>
###xml 32 42 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 705 710 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
BPTF, the mammalian ortholog of Drosophila NURF301, is a large, multi-domain protein that is apparently exclusive to the mammalian NURF complex (Figure S1A) [12],[15],[25]. An initial characterization of Bptf showed it to be nuclear in the P19 embryonic carcinoma cell line and can exist in at least two electrophoretic variants, which we termed Bptf-H and Bptf-L (Figure S1B, Figure S1C). As previously reported, Bptf is highly expressed in testis, spleen, brain and to a lesser extent in kidney by Western blotting (Figure S1D). Interestingly Bptf is highly expressed during embryonic development, and expression substantially declines upon birth (Figure S1E). The high levels of Bptf expression in the mouse embryo suggest it may have essential functions during embryonic development.
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 160 165 160 165 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 156 165 156 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 275 279 275 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 281 323 281 323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s002">Figure S2A, Figure S2B, S2C, S2D, S2E, S2F</xref>
###xml 326 331 326 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</italic>
###xml 335 339 335 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Stryke1">[26]</xref>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 629 633 629 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 670 692 670 692 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s003">Figure S3A, Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 790 794 790 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 799 845 799 842 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-galactosidase-neomycin phosphotransferase</italic>
###xml 847 853 844 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-G</italic>
###xml 893 903 887 897 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s003">Figure S3C</xref>
###xml 1006 1010 1000 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1019 1032 1013 1023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf&#8211;&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 1159 1169 1150 1160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s003">Figure S3D</xref>
###xml 1171 1175 1162 1166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Jones1">[25]</xref>
###xml 1285 1289 1273 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1355 1360 1343 1348 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 1351 1360 1339 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 119 124 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To elucidate the biological functions of mammalian Bptf during mammalian embryonic development we generated two mutant mouse lines. One line, designated as BptfXG023, was derived from an ES cell line carrying an in-frame gene-trap vector insertion between exons 15 and 16 of Bptf (Figure S2A, Figure S2B, S2C, S2D, S2E, S2F) (XG023; ) [26]. We identified the precise junction of the insertion site of the gene trap by DNA sequence analysis of the corresponding PCR products, and confirmed by RT-PCR that trapping of Bptf mRNA into vector sequences leads to loss of RNA splicing between exons 15 and 16, and reduced expression of Bptf sequences 3' to the insertion site (Figure S3A, Figure S3B). In addition, we confirmed by 5'-RACE that the insertion resulted in an in-frame fusion between Bptf and beta-galactosidase-neomycin phosphotransferase (beta-Geo) sequences of the gene-trap vector. (Figure S3C). Consistent with previous findings, Northern blotting of adult tissue RNA showed that both wild-type Bptf and the Bptf-beta-Geo fusion alleles are specifically expressed at high levels in the testis and at moderate levels in the lung, spleen, and brain (Figure S3D) [25]. These identical RNA expression patterns initially suggest that beta-galactosidase is a faithful reporter of Bptf expression in adult tissues. These results indicate that the BptfXG023 mutation creates a truncated Bptf-beta-Geo fusion carrying the N-terminal 1978 residues of the 2903-residue Bptf open reading frame, which eliminates the conserved glutamine rich region, PHD finger, and bromo-domains.
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 35 45 35 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 31 45 31 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 104 108 100 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 110 216 106 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s002">Figure S2A, Figure S2G, Figure S2H, Figure S2I, Figure S2J, Figure S2K, Figure S2L, Figure S2M, Figure S2N</xref>
###xml 245 255 241 247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 241 255 237 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 359 363 351 355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 398 408 390 396 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 394 408 386 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 449 453 437 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 472 482 460 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s004">Figure S4A</xref>
###xml 534 544 522 528 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 530 544 518 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 623 633 607 613 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 619 633 603 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 672 694 652 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s004">Figure S4B, Figure S4C</xref>
The second line, designated as BptfDeltaExon2, was generated by targeting loxP sites flanking exon 2 of Bptf (Figure S2A, Figure S2G, Figure S2H, Figure S2I, Figure S2J, Figure S2K, Figure S2L, Figure S2M, Figure S2N). The expression of the BptfDeltaExon2 allele was assessed by RT-PCR with the use of primer sets which amplify sequences on the 3' end of the Bptf transcript. We found that the BptfDeltaExon2 allele slightly decreases expression of Bptf at the RNA level (Figure S4A). However, amplification and sequencing of the BptfDeltaExon2 mRNA from exons 1 to 8 shows an out-of-frame mutant mRNA, indicating that BptfDeltaExon2 behaves as a loss-of-function allele (Figure S4B, Figure S4C).
###end p 15
###begin title 16
###xml 32 36 32 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Post-Implantation Phenotypes of Bptf Mutant Embryos
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 74 78 74 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 141 146 141 146 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 137 146 137 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 178 188 178 184 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 174 188 174 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 271 275 267 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 498 506 494 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s026">Table S1</xref>
###xml 29 33 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 86 91 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 114 118 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 161 165 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 238 242 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 292 297 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
We intercrossed heterozygous mice to determine the biological function of Bptf during mouse development. With 210 mice genotyped for the BptfXG023 allele and 75 mice for the BptfDeltaExon2 allele, we did not find any surviving homozygous mice at weaning, indicating that Bptf is required for mouse development. An analysis of E6.5 to E18.5 progeny derived from heterozygous intercrosses confirmed that the homozygous mutant phenotype is embryonic-lethal between E7.5 to E8.5, with 100% penetrance (Table S1).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 56 61 56 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 52 61 52 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 70 80 70 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 66 80 66 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 222 231 218 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 234 244 230 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s005">Figure S5A</xref>
###xml 404 409 400 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 400 409 396 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 418 428 414 420 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 414 428 410 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 486 491 478 483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 482 491 474 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 496 506 488 494 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 492 506 484 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 583 588 571 576 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 579 588 567 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 597 607 585 591 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 593 607 581 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 684 694 668 678 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s005">Figure S5B</xref>
###xml 888 893 872 877 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 884 893 868 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 902 912 886 892 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 898 912 882 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 1024 1028 1004 1008 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1159 1168 1139 1148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 1285 1289 1265 1269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Wang1">[27]</xref>
###xml 1290 1294 1270 1274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Hamatani1">[28]</xref>
###xml 442 446 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To identify defects in the embryonic development of BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaExon2 homozygotes, we performed whole mount examinations of mutant embryos. Growth defects increasing in severity from E5.5 to E7.5 were observed (Figure 1A) (Figure S5A). Dissections conducted at E8.5 and E9.5 were uninformative, because a majority of the embryos had been completely reabsorbed (data not shown). We crossed BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaExon2 heterozygous mice to generate the trans-heterozygous BptfXG023/BptfDeltaExon2 embryos. The trans-heterozygote recapitulated the growth defects of the BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaExon2 homozygotes, indicating that the two mutations are functionally equivalent (Figure S5B). To determine whether the developmental defects originated before implantation, we harvested E3.5 blastocysts and performed blastocyst outgrowth assays. We observed normal E3.5 homozygous BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaExon2 blastocysts and normal outgrowths from the blastocysts after tissue culture for 5 days, suggesting that either Bptf is not essential for pre-implantation development or that the maternal Bptf protein or mRNA can mask pre-implantation phenotypes (Figure S6). The masking of pre-implantation phenotypes by maternal Bptf is possible because it is highly expressed in oocytes [27],[28].
###end p 18
###begin title 19
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Bptf mutants manifest early embryonic growth defects.
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 66 71 66 71 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 61 71 61 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf <sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 234 239 234 239 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 229 239 229 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf <sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 522 526 522 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 772 777 772 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf-</italic>
(A) Wild type (+/+), heterozygous (+/-), and homozygous (-/-)Bptf XG023 embryos at E5.5, E6.5, and E7.5 were removed from their decedua and genotyped using the PCR based method. Reduced growth rates are evident in the homozygous Bptf XG023 embryos as early as E5.5. (B) Hematoxylin and eosin (H&E) staining of E5.5, E6.5, and E7.5 mutant embryos show reduced growth of both embryonic and extra-embryonic tissues, the presence of visceral endoderm, and an absence of anterior-posterior asymmetry when compared to controls. Bptf mutant embryos were stained for phosphorylated histone H3, a marker of cell mitosis. Mutant embryos at E5.5, E6.5, and E7.5 have significantly reduced staining when compared to controls, suggesting that they have reduced cellular proliferation. Bptf-mutant embryos were stained for apoptotic cells using the TUNEL assay. Mutant embryos at E5.5, E6.5, and E7.5 do not have any positive staining by TUNEL when compared to controls, suggesting that they are not apoptotic. Scale Bars: E5.5 and E6.5 embryos = 50 microm, E7.5 embryos = 100 microm. Abbreviations: ve, visceral endoderm; ee, embryonic ectoderm; m, mesoderm; xe, extra-embryonic ectoderm; xve, extra-embryonic visceral endoderm.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 118 123 118 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 114 123 114 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 498 507 498 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 778 787 778 787 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
To further investigate the basis of the early embryonic lethal phenotype, we performed a histological analysis of BptfXG023 mutant embryos at E5.5, E6.5 and E7.5. Mid-sagittal sections of E5.5, E6.5 and E7.5 embryos stained with hematoxylin and eosin (H&E) showed a distinct proximal-distal (P-D) axis and the development of visceral endoderm but a significant decrease in size of the embryonic and extra-embryonic tissues. This was particularly evident in the embryonic ectoderm at E6.5 and E7.5 (Figure 1B). By E6.5, mutant embryos showed clear developmental defects. Although there was a clear boundary between extra embryonic and embryonic tissues, the absence of a primitive streak and any discernable mesoderm suggests that the anterior-posterior (A-P) axis did not form (Figure 1B).
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 340 349 340 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 476 485 476 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 685 694 673 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s007">Figure S7</xref>
A reduction in cell number can be a consequence of decreased cell proliferation, increased cell death (apoptosis), or a combination of both processes. To ascertain the extent of programmed cell death, we performed TUNEL assays on E5.5, E.6.5 and E7.5 homozygotes and found no increased numbers of apoptotic cells when compared to controls (Figure 1B). As a measure of cell proliferation we monitored phosphorylated histone H3 levels in the conceptus by immuno-histochemistry (Figure 1B). E5.5, E6.5 and E7.5 homozygotes showed approximately40-50% decrease in phosphorylated histone H3 levels indicating that a decrease in cellular proliferation may contribute to the mutant phenotype (Figure S7).
###end p 22
###begin title 23
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Bptf Mutants Fail To Develop a Functional Distal Visceral Endoderm
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 269 273 269 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tam1">[29]</xref>
###xml 447 452 447 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gata6</italic>
###xml 461 466 461 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nanog</italic>
###xml 466 470 466 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Chazaud1">[30]</xref>
###xml 832 836 814 818 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tam1">[29]</xref>
###xml 931 935 913 917 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-PereaGomez1">[31]</xref>
###xml 1080 1084 1062 1066 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tam1">[29]</xref>
###xml 34 39 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Subsequent to implantation of the mouse blastocyst there is rapid proliferation of the egg cylinder, which consists of three cell types: the more proximal extra-embryonic ectoderm, the more distal embryonic ectoderm or epiblast, and an outer layer of visceral endoderm [29]. The visceral endoderm originates from the primitive endoderm, a layer of cells organized at E4.5, which is composed of cells from the ICM of the E3.5 blastocyst expressing Gata6 but not Nanog[30]. At approximatelyE5.5, a specialized cluster of endoderm cells, the DVE, arises at the distal tip of the embryo. DVE cells migrate toward the prospective anterior, to form the anterior visceral endoderm (AVE). DVE/AVE cells secrete molecules such as cerberus (Cer1) and Lefty1, antagonists of the Transforming Growth Factor beta (TGFbeta)-related protein Nodal [29]. These antagonists restrict the activity of Nodal to the posterior pole of the embryo at E6.0 [31]. The primitive streak forms at E6.5, indicating that gastrulation has begun, and gives rise to the mesoderm and definitive endoderm germ layers [29].
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 105 109 105 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 116 123 116 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 302 306 302 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 361 370 361 370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 515 522 509 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 585 589 579 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 590 598 584 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 657 697 648 688 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s008">Figure S8A, S8B, S8C, S8D, S8E, S8F, S8G</xref>
###xml 756 760 747 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 761 769 752 757 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 914 938 902 926 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s008">Figure S8A&#8242;, Figure S8B&#8242;</xref>
###xml 1040 1044 1028 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1045 1053 1033 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 1091 1133 1076 1118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s009">Figure S9A, Figure S9B, S9C, S9D, S9E, S9F</xref>
###xml 1193 1197 1178 1182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1321 1325 1306 1310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 489 493 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
As a first step in the molecular analysis of Bptf in embryonic development we examined the expression of Bptf using in situ RNA hybridization. We observed expression in the inner cell mass (ICM) and primitive endoderm at E4.5 and all embryonic tissues at E5.5 and E6.5. Interestingly we do not observe Bptf expression in the visceral endoderm at E5.5 and E6.5 (Figure 2A). We also monitored the activity of the beta-galactosidase moiety of the Bptf-beta-Geo fusion protein in heterozygous mice. Consistent with our in situ analysis a histochemical analysis of whole mounts showed that Bptf-beta-Geo is expressed in the embryo proper at E5.5, E6.5 and E7.5 (Figure S8A, S8B, S8C, S8D, S8E, S8F, S8G). Further analysis of histological sections revealed that Bptf-beta-Geo expression at E7.5 is primarily confined to the embryonic ectoderm, with reduced levels in mesoderm and no expression in the visceral endoderm (Figure S8A', Figure S8B'). At subsequent stages, from E7.5 to E13.5, histochemical analysis of whole mounts showed widespread Bptf-beta-Geo expression in the developing embryo (Figure S9A, Figure S9B, S9C, S9D, S9E, S9F). This temporal correlation between the earliest stages of Bptf expression and the stages when the mutant phenotype is revealed, suggests that there could be an essential requirement for Bptf as early as E4.5.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Bptf mutants are defective in the expression of distal visceral endoderm markers.
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 54 58 54 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 67 74 67 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 118 122 118 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 404 411 404 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 489 501 489 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nanog, Gata6</italic>
###xml 503 515 503 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lefty1, Cer1</italic>
###xml 517 522 517 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1,</italic>
###xml 527 532 527 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 554 558 554 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 593 605 593 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nanog, Gata6</italic>
###xml 607 614 607 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lefty1,</italic>
###xml 619 624 619 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1,</italic>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 779 783 779 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer1</italic>
###xml 788 793 788 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1,</italic>
###xml 891 896 891 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GATA6</italic>
(A) Wild type embryos were stained in whole mount for Bptf mRNA by in situ RNA hybridization at E4.5, E5.5, and E6.5. Bptf is expressed in the inner cell mass and primitive endoderm at E4.5 and in the embryonic and extra-embryonic tissues in E5.5 and E6.5 embryos. Abbreviations: ve, visceral endoderm; ee, embryonic ectoderm; xe, extra-embryonic ectoderm; DVE, distal visceral endoderm. (B) Whole mount in situ RNA hybridization analysis of wild type and mutant E4.5 and E5.5 embryos for Nanog, Gata6, Lefty1, Cer1, Hex1, and Nodal expression. At E4.5, Bptf mutant embryos show expression of Nanog, Gata6, Lefty1, and Hex1, suggesting that the primitive endoderm and inner cell mass is present in Bptf mutants. Mutant E5.5 embryos are defective in the expression of DVE markers Cer1 and Hex1, suggesting that mutants cannot form the DVE. Interestingly, the general visceral endoderm marker GATA6 is not expressed in the VE but rather in the embryonic ectoderm at E5.5.
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 192 196 192 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tam1">[29]</xref>
###xml 291 336 291 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Otx2, Lefty1, Cer1, Hesx1, Hex1, Gata6, Nanog</italic>
###xml 341 346 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 350 357 350 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 403 407 403 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Chambers1">[32]</xref>
###xml 408 412 408 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-PereaGomez2">[37]</xref>
Our histological analysis suggests that Bptf mutants are defective in establishing an A-P axis. Apparent defects in A-P axis can be due to defects in the establishment or migration of the DVE [29]. To monitor the development of the DVE and its transition to the AVE, we analyzed the markers Otx2, Lefty1, Cer1, Hesx1, Hex1, Gata6, Nanog and Nodal by in situ hybridization in E4.5 to E6.5 mutant embryos [32]-[37].
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 55 59 55 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 143 147 143 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 215 229 215 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gata6, Lefty1,</italic>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1</italic>
###xml 283 292 283 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 341 345 341 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 585 590 585 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nanog</italic>
###xml 594 598 594 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 629 638 629 638 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 685 689 685 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
An analysis of pre-implantation embryos suggested that Bptf mutants specify a functional primitive endoderm and ICM. The primitive endoderm of Bptf mutant embryos was found to express the primitive endoderm markers Gata6, Lefty1, and Hex1 at comparable levels to wild type controls (Figure 3B). The expression of these markers suggests that Bptf mutants are not defective in the differentiation of the primitive endoderm, the precursor of the visceral endoderm of E5.5 and later stage embryos. Consistent with a functional ICM, we observed normal expression of the pluripotency marker Nanog in Bptf mutants compared to controls (Figure 2B). Taken together, these results indicate that Bptf is not required for the specification of the primitive endoderm and the ICM in E4.5 embryos.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 12 16 12 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 26 31 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Analysis of Bptf knockout mouse embryonic stem cells shows severe defects in gene expression during embryoid differentiation.
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 224 228 224 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Relative expression of developmental markers during an embryoid body differentiation time course. The expression of many markers of the ectoderm (A), mesoderm (B), and endoderm (C) tissue lineages were severely defective in Bptf mutants during the differentiation time course.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 78 96 78 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer1, Hex1, Gata6,</italic>
###xml 101 106 101 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 115 119 115 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 165 175 165 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer1, Hex1</italic>
###xml 205 209 205 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 254 263 254 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 364 368 364 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 384 389 384 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gata6</italic>
###xml 522 531 522 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 553 557 553 557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 661 666 661 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 668 673 668 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 813 817 813 817 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Takaoka1">[36]</xref>
###xml 818 822 818 822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Mesnard1">[38]</xref>
###xml 832 836 832 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 891 896 891 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 945 956 945 956 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s010">Figure S10A</xref>
###xml 980 985 980 985 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 1020 1024 1020 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1041 1052 1041 1052 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s010">Figure S10B</xref>
To assess the specification of the VE and DVE, we monitored the expression of Cer1, Hex1, Gata6, and Nodal in E5.5 Bptf mutant embryos. We observed that the markers Cer1, Hex1 are significantly reduced in Bptf mutants relative to the wild type controls (Figure 2B). The absence of expression of these markers indicates that the DVE does not form in the absence of Bptf. Interestingly Gata6 expression, normally expressed only in the VE at E5.5 and E6.5, is absent in the VE but present in the epiblast in mutants at E5.5 (Figure 2B). This suggests that Bptf could also have roles in specifying the VE as well as the DVE. A key regulator of DVE specification is Nodal. Nodal expression is found as early as E4.5 but is not significantly expressed in the epiblast and VE until implantation is well underway at E5.0 [36],[38]. In E5.5 Bptf mutant embryos we observe normal expression levels of Nodal in the epiblast and VE as in wild type embryos (Figure S10A). This E5.5 pattern of Nodal expression continues into E6.5 in Bptf mutant embryos (Figure S10B).
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 69 94 69 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer1, Otx2, Hesx1, Lefty1</italic>
###xml 99 103 99 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1</italic>
###xml 112 116 112 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 133 137 133 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Otx2</italic>
###xml 244 248 244 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Otx2</italic>
###xml 268 272 268 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 326 337 326 337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A</xref>
###xml 397 416 397 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer1, Hesx1, Lefty1</italic>
###xml 421 425 421 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hex1</italic>
###xml 429 433 429 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 450 461 450 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A</xref>
To examine the development of the AVE we monitored the expression of Cer1, Otx2, Hesx1, Lefty1 and Hex1 in E6.5 Bptf mutant embryos. Otx2 expression is required for the migration of the DVE to establish the AVE. We observed lower expression of Otx2 in the epiblast of Bptf mutant embryos relative to there wild type controls (Figure S11A). As expected we did not observe expression of AVE markers Cer1, Hesx1, Lefty1 and Hex1 in Bptf mutant embryos (Figure S11A). Combined with our analysis of E5.5 embryos our results strongly suggest that Bptf is required for the speciation of the DVE and the AVE.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 276 283 276 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T, Lhx1</italic>
###xml 285 289 285 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgf8</italic>
###xml 291 294 291 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gsc</italic>
###xml 296 309 296 309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Foxa2, Nodal,</italic>
###xml 314 320 314 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cripto</italic>
###xml 322 327 322 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Tdgf1</italic>
###xml 423 427 423 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Varlet1">[34]</xref>
###xml 429 433 429 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Ding1">[39]</xref>
###xml 434 438 434 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Sun1">[42]</xref>
###xml 467 474 467 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T, Lhx1</italic>
###xml 476 480 476 480 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgf8</italic>
###xml 482 485 482 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gsc</italic>
###xml 491 496 491 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Foxa2</italic>
###xml 543 544 543 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</italic>
###xml 546 550 546 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgf8</italic>
###xml 559 563 559 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lhx1</italic>
###xml 605 629 605 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A, Figure S11B</xref>
###xml 824 828 824 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 869 874 869 874 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 879 885 879 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cripto</italic>
###xml 922 926 922 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1034 1043 1034 1043 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 1046 1057 1046 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A</xref>
###xml 1060 1071 1060 1071 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s010">Figure S10A</xref>
###xml 1073 1084 1073 1084 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11B</xref>
###xml 1086 1090 1086 1090 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Varlet1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1091 1095 1091 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Ding1">[39]</xref>
###xml 1136 1140 1136 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Since Bptf mutant embryos are unable to form a functional DVE and AVE, we anticipated that they should be defective in specifying the primitive streak and differentiating mesoderm and definitive endoderm. Several critical transcription factors and signaling molecules such as T, Lhx1, Fgf8, Gsc, Foxa2, Nodal, and Cripto (Tdgf1) serve as effective markers for development of the primitive streak in the gastrulating embryo [34], [39]-[42]. Our analyses revealed that T, Lhx1, Fgf8, Gsc, and Foxa2 were undetectable at E6.5, and in the case of T, Fgf8 but not Lhx1, were delocalized in expression at E7.5 (Figure S11A, Figure S11B). The absence of expression of primitive streak markers at E6.5 confirms our histological analyses, and further supports the observation that gastrulation and mesoderm formation do not occur in Bptf mutants. Interestingly, the delocalized Nodal and Cripto expression patterns observed in the Bptf mutants at E6.5 are highly reminiscent of their expression patterns prior to the establishment of the DVE (Figure 2B) (Figure S11A) (Figure S10A, Figure S11B) [34],[39]. Taken together, the data suggests that Bptf mutant embryos arrest at a stage prior to DVE formation (<E5.5).
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 144 148 144 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tam1">[29]</xref>
###xml 198 202 198 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 381 385 381 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bmp4</italic>
###xml 387 399 387 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Erbb2, Fgfr2</italic>
###xml 417 422 417 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mash2</italic>
###xml 439 443 439 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vegf</italic>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Flk1</italic>
###xml 479 483 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">JunB</italic>
###xml 493 497 493 497 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Winnier1">[43]</xref>
###xml 498 502 498 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Miquerol1">[47]</xref>
###xml 512 531 512 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bmp4, Mash2, Erbb2,</italic>
###xml 536 541 536 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgfr2</italic>
###xml 607 631 607 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A, Figure S11B</xref>
###xml 684 688 684 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 844 848 844 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vegf</italic>
###xml 853 857 853 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Flk1</italic>
###xml 898 909 898 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11B</xref>
###xml 960 964 960 964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">JunB</italic>
###xml 1044 1055 1044 1055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s011">Figure S11A</xref>
###xml 1058 1062 1058 1062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">JunB</italic>
###xml 1172 1176 1172 1176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Shaulian1">[48]</xref>
###xml 1200 1204 1200 1204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">JunB</italic>
###xml 1246 1250 1246 1250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1296 1305 1296 1305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000241-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 1308 1317 1308 1317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s007">Figure S7</xref>
Recent models propose that the extra-embryonic ectoderm supports the growth of the embryo and is a source of signals for A-P axis establishment [29]. To address whether the developmental defects of Bptf mutants are caused by defective extra-embryonic ectoderm or by a lack of appropriate growth signals in the epiblast, we monitored the expression of the extra embryonic ectoderm (Bmp4, Erbb2, Fgfr2), trophectoderm (Mash2), angiogenesis (Vegf, Flk1) and a cell cycle regulator (JunB) markers [43]-[47]. We find Bmp4, Mash2, Erbb2, and Fgfr2 to be expressed normally in the mutant embryos at E6.5 and E7.5 (Figure S11A, Figure S11B). This suggests that the growth defects observed in Bptf embryos are not due to gross defects in the specification the extra-embryonic tissues. We also observe little to no expression of the angiogenesis markers Vegf and Flk1 in the extra-embryonic tissues at E7.5 (Figure S11B). However, expression of the cell cycle regulator JunB is increased in mutant embryonic ectoderm when compared to wild-type controls (Figure S11A). JunB is a member of the Ap-1 family of transcription factors which acts as a negative regulator of the cell cycle [48]. This up-regulation of JunB is consistent with our observations that Bptf mutants have reduced cellular proliferation (Figure 1B) (Figure S7).
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 47 54 47 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 108 112 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 454 458 454 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
In summary, our analysis of lineage markers by in situ RNA hybridization has revealed an essential role for Bptf in specifying the VE and the DVE of the E5.5 post implantation embryo. These defects likely lead to the observed absence of an AVE and primitive streak in E6.5 embryos. The absence of these developmental organizers arrests the growth of the embryo prior to gastrulation and is likely a major cause of the early embryonic lethal phenotype of Bptf mutant embryos.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Bptf Is Required for Embryonic Stem Cell Differentiation
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 133 141 133 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 146 153 146 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 260 270 260 266 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 256 270 256 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 320 331 316 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s012">Figure S12A</xref>
###xml 373 377 369 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 478 489 474 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s012">Figure S12B</xref>
###xml 511 521 507 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 507 521 503 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 682 706 674 698 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s012">Figure S12C, Figure S12D</xref>
###xml 87 92 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To further explore the role of Bptf in cell differentiation we generated Bptf knockout mouse ES cells and examined their development in vitro and in vivo. By gene targeting and transient Cre expression we were able to generate eight independent homozygous BptfDeltaExon2 knockout ES cell lines with a euploid karyotype (Figure S12A). We observed varying degrees of reduced Bptf transcript levels by Northern blotting in mutant cell lines compared to that of wild type controls (Figure S12B). An analysis of BptfDeltaExon2 mRNA from exons 1 to 8 in wild type and knockout cell lines shows the message to be out of frame resulting in no observable protein in the knockout cell lines (Figure S12C, Figure S12D) (data not shown).
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 128 132 128 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 156 166 156 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s013">Figure S13</xref>
###xml 178 182 178 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 281 291 281 291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s014">Figure S14</xref>
###xml 318 322 318 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
To address the possibility the Bptf is essential for cell viability and proliferation we measured the doubling time of knockout Bptf ES and MEF cell lines (Figure S13). Both the Bptf knockout ES and MEF cell lines were viable but exhibited slightly reduced cellular proliferation (Figure S14). These results show that Bptf is not required for cell viability and is only marginally required for cellular proliferation.
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 49 53 49 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 72 80 72 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 104 111 104 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 332 336 332 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 451 455 451 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 224 228 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 326 330 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We measured the differentiation potential of the Bptf knockout ES cells in vitro as embryoid bodies and in vivo as teratomas. Bptf wild type and two independent knockout cell lines were subcutaneously injected into NOD/SCID mice and allowed to form teratomas over 8 weeks. Wild type ES cells formed teratomas in 8/11 injected mice. Bptf knockout lines did not form any observable tumors in 10 injections (data not shown). This study demonstrated that Bptf is essential for one or more biological processes including cell viability, proliferation or differentiation in the animal.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 309 320 309 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s015">Figure S15A</xref>
###xml 343 347 343 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 445 469 445 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s015">Figure S15B, Figure S15C</xref>
###xml 500 504 500 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
We next utilized an embryoid body analysis to monitor differentiation in Bptf knockout cell lines to ectoderm, mesoderm and endoderm cell lineages. Analysis of the mutant embryoid bodies showed little evidence of apoptosis by TUNEL, and similar densities of PCNA and phosphorylated histone H3 positive cells (Figure S15A). We did observe that Bptf knockout embryoid bodies were slightly smaller in size and did not form any observable endoderm (Figure S15B, Figure S15C). These results indicate that Bptf is not necessary for cellular survival or proliferation under conditions of embryoid body differentiation but is essential for differentiation of endoderm and possibly other advanced tissue lineages.
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
