###begin title 80
Southern Blotting Genotyping Procedures
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 130 134 130 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
###xml 906 914 884 892 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 673 678 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Mice were routinely genotyped by Southern blotting restriction digested tail DNA. Tail DNA was prepared using standard procedures [67]. approximately10 microg of DNA was digested with the appropriate restriction enzyme and resolved by 0.5% agarose gel electrophoresis for standard electrophoresis or 1.0% agarose using FIGE. DNA was transferred to Hybond XL (Amersham) using alkaline capillary transfer crosslinked with UV (Stratalinker) and probed with random hexamer labeled probes at 65degreesC using Perfect Hyb Hybridization Buffer (Sigma). Probes used for blotting were PCR amplified from pCH110 (Genbank # UO2445) using primers JL510 and JL511 for Probe B, and from mouse genomic DNA using primers JL299 and JL300 for Probe A; JL60 and JL61 for probe exon2; JL235 and JL236 for probe 29-31; JL293 and JL294 for probe 25-26; JL295 and JL296 for probe 20.2-20.7 using Taq polymerase (Invitrogen) (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Blots were washed twice with 2.0x SSC, 0.1% SDS and twice with 0.5x SSC, 0.1% SDS for 10 min @ 65degreesC for each wash. A Phosphoimager was used to detect the hybridization signal.
###end p 81
###begin title 82
PCR Genotyping Procedures
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 87 92 87 92 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 83 92 83 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 177 185 177 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 311 312 307 308 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 704 708 666 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 727 732 689 694 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 723 732 685 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
Embryos were genotyped using a PCR based strategy. Primers used for genotyping the BptfXG023 line were as follows, Primer A (JL511), Primer B (JL627), and Primer C (JL631) (see Table S3 for primer sequences). PCR reactions were performed in 25 microl volumes with 20 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.4), 50 mM KCl, 1.5 mM MgCl2, 0.2 mM each dNTP, 0.2 microM each primer, 1 Unit Taq Polymerase (Invitrogen). Reactions were heated for 3 min at 94degreesC, and then cycled for 35 cycles at 30 sec at 94degreesC, 30 sec at 65degreesC, and 45 sec at 72degreesC, followed by one cycle for 2 min at 72degreesC. PCR products were resolved on 1.5% agarose gels. The genotype of embryos was confirmed by the presence of a 250 bp Bptf and/or 500 bp BptfXG023 bands.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 62 72 62 68 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;exon2</sup>
###xml 58 72 58 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 196 204 192 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 330 331 322 323 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 719 723 677 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 736 742 694 700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Floxed</sup>
###xml 732 742 690 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>Floxed</sup></italic>
###xml 751 760 709 718 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FloxedNeo</sup>
###xml 747 760 705 718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>FloxedNeo</sup></italic>
###xml 771 775 729 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 780 785 734 739 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exon2</sup>
###xml 780 785 734 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>exon2</sup></italic>
Two different PCR strategies were used for genotyping the BptfDeltaexon2 line. The primers used in the first strategy are as follows, Primer A (JL648), Primer B (JL649), and Primer C (JL652) (see Table S3 for primer sequences). PCR reactions were performed in 25 microl volumes with 20 mM Tris-HCL (pH 8.4), 50 mM KCl, 1.5 mM MgCl2, 0.2 mM each dNTP, 0.2 microM each primer, 1 Unit Taq Polymerase (Invitrogen). Reactions were heated for 3 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 35 cycles at 30 sec at 94degreesC, 30 sec at 60degreesC, and 45 sec at 72degreesC, followed by one cycle for 2 min at 72degreesC. PCR products were resolved on 1.5% agarose gels. The genotype of embryos was confirmed by the presence of a 250 bp Bptf, 325 bp BptfFloxed and BptfFloxedNeo or 550 bp BptfDeltaexon2 band.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 116 124 116 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 250 251 246 247 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 639 643 601 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 656 662 618 624 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Floxed</sup>
###xml 652 662 614 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>Floxed</sup></italic>
###xml 673 677 635 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 682 687 640 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exon2</sup>
###xml 682 687 640 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>exon2</sup></italic>
The primers used in the second method are as follows, Primer C (JL651), Primer E (JL655), and Primer F (JL662) (see Table S3 for primer sequences). PCR reactions were performed in 25 microl volumes with 20 mM Tris-HCL (pH 8.4), 50 mM KCl, 1.5 mM MgCl2, 0.2 mM each dNTP, 0.2 microM each primer, 1 Unit Taq Polymerase (Invitrogen). Reactions were heated for 3 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 35 cycles at 30 sec at 94degreesC, 30 sec at 65degreesC, and 45 sec at 72degreesC, followed by one cycle for 2 min at 72degreesC. PCR products were resolved on 1.5% agarose gels. The genotype of embryos was confirmed by the presence of a 375 bp Bptf, 475 bp BptfFloxed or 650 bp BptfDeltaexon2 bands.
###end p 85
###begin p 86
###xml 15 20 15 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 11 20 11 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 25 29 25 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 34 39 30 35 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exon2</sup>
###xml 34 39 30 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 71 75 67 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 92 102 88 94 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;exon2</sup>
###xml 88 102 84 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 185 189 177 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 229 239 221 227 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;exon2</sup>
###xml 225 239 217 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 342 346 330 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 426 431 414 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAPDH</italic>
###xml 457 462 445 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAPDH</italic>
###xml 479 483 467 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 504 509 492 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAPDH</italic>
###xml 514 518 502 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 644 649 626 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAPDH</italic>
###xml 668 672 650 654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 924 925 884 885 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1009 1017 965 973 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
To confirm BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaexon2 expression and an out of frame Bptf mRNA in the BptfDeltaexon2 line we designed primers with homology to the 3' end and exons 1 through 8 of the Bptf mRNA. Total RNA from wild type and BptfDeltaexon2 homozygous embryos was converted to cDNA using superscript II according to manufacturer's procedures. Bptf expression was estimated by first normalizing cDNA to equal concentration with GAPDH amplification. Following GAPDH normalization 3'Bptf was amplified. Both GAPDH and Bptf were amplified in the linear range as follows. Reactions were heated for 10 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 22 cycles for GAPDH and 30 cycles for Bptf at 20 sec at 94degreesC, 20 sec at 60degreesC, and 30 sec at 72degreesC. PCR products were resolved by native PAGE. The exon 1-8 junction was amplified using primers P3 and JL15 in 25 microl volumes with 20 mM Tris-HCL (pH 8.4), 50 mM KCl, 1.5 mM MgCl2, 0.2 mM each dNTP, 0.2 microM each primer, 1 Unit Taq Polymerase (Invitrogen) (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Reactions were heated for 3 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 35 cycles at 30 sec at 94degreesC, 30 sec at 65degreesC, and 2 min at 72degreesC, followed by one cycle for 5 min at 72degreesC. PCR products were resolved on 1.5% agarose gels. PCR fragments were cloned using TOPO TA cloning system (Invitrogen) and sequenced with Big Dye V3.1 using M13 forward and reverse primers.
###end p 86
###begin p 87
###xml 39 44 39 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 35 44 35 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 238 246 238 246 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 618 623 576 581 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 614 623 572 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 160 165 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The exact integration site for the BptfXG023 insertion allele was confirmed by sequencing a PCR product generated by amplifying genomic DNA from a heterozygous mouse tail clipping. The DNA was amplified using primers JL511 and JL515 (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Reactions were heated for 3 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 35 cycles at 30 sec at 94degreesC, 30 sec at 65degreesC, and 60 sec at 72degreesC, followed by one cycle for 2 min at 72degreesC. A approximately1.8 Kb PCR product was resolved on 1.5% agarose and purified. The product was sequenced using Big Dye v3.1 using primer JL511 to obtain BptfXG023 junction sequence.
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 4 9 4 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 0 9 0 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 96 101 96 101 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 87 101 87 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf/Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
BptfXG023 disruption was confirmed by 5' RACE according to established procedures from Bptf/BptfXG023 total testis RNA according to procedures established by the Bay Genomics Gene Trap Consortium (). Two separate 5' RACE reactions were sequenced giving identical results.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
Embryo Procedures
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 83 87 83 87 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
Timed pregnancies used to collect embryos were preformed using standard procedures [67]. Embryonic day 0.5 was recorded the morning after an observable plug was found. Portions of later stage E18.5 to E10.5 embryos were genotyped by Southern blotting and early E9.5 to E3.5 embryos and outgrowths were genotyped by PCR.
###end p 90
###begin p 91
###xml 46 53 43 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 253 260 247 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 304 308 298 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
###xml 365 372 359 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 447 451 441 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
###xml 519 520 513 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</italic>
###xml 522 541 516 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lhx1, GATA6, Lefty1</italic>
###xml 543 547 537 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FGF4</italic>
###xml 549 553 543 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FGF8</italic>
###xml 555 560 549 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HesX1</italic>
###xml 562 566 556 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hhex</italic>
###xml 568 574 562 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cripto</italic>
###xml 576 580 570 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BMP4</italic>
###xml 582 586 576 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Otx2</italic>
###xml 588 593 582 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nodal</italic>
###xml 595 598 589 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cer</italic>
###xml 600 637 594 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Foxa2, Erb2, Fgfr2, Mash1, JunB, VEGF</italic>
###xml 642 646 636 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Flk1</italic>
###xml 648 655 642 649 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In situ</italic>
###xml 991 995 976 980 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
###xml 1056 1063 1038 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
Embryos used for beta-galactosidase staining, in situ hybridizations and phenotypic analysis were dissected from their deciduas in PBS at room temperature prior to staining/hybridization. Embryos were stained for beta-galactosidase activity or used for in situ hybridizations using established protocols [67] (T. Yamaguchi, personal communication). Probes used for in situ RNA hybridizations were labeled with DIG according to standard procedures [67]. Plasmids or PCR products used for probe synthesis were as follows T, Lhx1, GATA6, Lefty1, FGF4, FGF8, HesX1, Hhex, Cripto, BMP4, Otx2, Nodal, Cer, Foxa2, Erb2, Fgfr2, Mash1, JunB, VEGF and Flk1. In situ signals were detected using BM Purple AP Substrate according to manufactures instructions (Roche). Embryos selected for sectioning were post fixed in 4% PFA overnight at 4degreesC, dehydrated in alcohol and embedded in paraffin and sectioned after beta-galactosidase staining. Sectioned embryos were obtained using standard techniques [67]. Embryos genotyped following beta-galactosidase staining or in situ hybridization were prepared post staining by digesting the embryo proper overnight at 55degreesC in 10 to 20 microl PBS, 0.1% tween 20, 2 mg/ml PCR grade protenase K (Roche). Proteinase K was heat inactivated at 100degreesC for 15 min and 2 microl was subsequently used for PCR genotyping.
###end p 91
###begin p 92
###xml 395 399 389 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Nagy1">[67]</xref>
Deciduas used for sectioning were dissected from the uterus in PBS, washed once with PBS and immersed in 4% PFA buffered with PBS overnight at 4degreesC. Deciduas were then dehydrated in an ethanol series and imbedded in paraffin. Paraffin blocks were trimmed and sectioned and sections were stained with hematoxylin and eosin, TUNEL assay and phosphorylated H3 according to standard procedures [67].
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 264 271 264 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ex vivo</italic>
Embryos used for RT PCR analysis were dissected in DMEM, 25 mM HEPES pH 7.4, 15% FCS, 2 mM glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin. Embryonic and extra embryonic tissue was removed from the ectoplacental cone and frozen in dry ice. The ectoplacental cone was grown ex vivo in DMEM, 15% FCS, glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin using standard culture conditions. After 4 days growth extra embryonic cells were removed from the outgrowth and subjected to PCR genotyping as described above and qPCR as described below.
###end p 93
###begin p 94
Outgrowth assays were preformed on E3.5 blastocysts. E3.5 blastocysts were isolated in 15% FCS, M2, 10 microM mercapto-ethanol, penicillin and streptomycin using standard procedures. Blastocysts were then transferred to gelatinized plates containing 15% FCS, M16, 10 microM beta-mercaptoethanol, 2 mM glutamine with penicillin and streptomycin. Outgrowths were cultured under standard conditions for 5 days and observed for defects. At the end of the experiment the outgrowths were removed and genotyped by PCR using conditions above.
###end p 94
###begin title 95
Tissue Extraction
###end title 95
###begin p 96
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 51 55 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Mouse tissues were extracted from 3 month old male mice sacrificed by CO2 asphixation and immediately frozen in liquid nitrogen. Tissues were then extracted using TriReagent (Sigma) according to manufacturers established procedures. RNA precipitate was extensively washed in 80% EtOH, re-suspended in DEPC treated water and stored at -80degreesC. Protein precipitate was extensively washed with 0.3 M guanadininum hydrochloride, 95% ethanol and re-suspended in 8M urea, 1% SDS and stored at -80degreesC. Protein concentration was determined using the DC Protein Assay (BioRad) according to manufacturer's procedures.
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
mRNA from embryos successfully genotyped as WT or Bptf-/- from ectoplacental growth outgrowths was isolated using Quick Prep Micro mRNA Purification Kit (Amersham).
###end p 97
###begin title 98
Northern Blotting
###end title 98
###begin p 99
RNA samples were denatured, resolved by formaldehyde agarose electrophoresis and blotted to Gene Screen (Dupont) by high salt capillary transfer according to standard procedures. Blots were probed with random hexamer labeled DNA probes using Prefect Hyb hybridization solution (Sigma) at 65degreesC according to the manufactures procedures. Probes used were the Probe B and Exon2 probe described above. Blots were washed with four times with 1x SSC for 10 minutes at 65degreesC. Phosphoimager was used to detect the hybridization signal.
###end p 99
###begin title 100
Western Blotting
###end title 100
###begin p 101
###xml 314 318 310 314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Wysocka1">[14]</xref>
###xml 530 536 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 540 545 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Protein samples were diluted in SDS sample buffer and resolved by PAGE. 50 microg total protein was transferred to PVDF (Biorad) using 10 mM CAPS, pH 10.5, 15% methanol, 3.5 mM DTT transfer solution for 17 hours at 20 mA and 20 V limits. Membranes were blotted with affinity purified anti-Bptf at 1:10000 dilution [14], M2 anti Flag monoclonal antibody at 1:5000 (Sigma), anti Smad2 and Smad2-phos (Cell Signaling Technologies) 1:1000, anti SNF2H/L (Abcam) 1:5000, anti-CBP and p300 1:100 (Abcam) overnight at 4degreesC then anti rabbit or mouse HRP (Amersham) at 1:20000 dilution for 2 hrs at RT in PBS with 5% NFDM and 0.1% tween 20 through out.
###end p 101
###begin p 102
###xml 470 476 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 700 706 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Histone Western blotting was performed essentially as above. Protein samples were extracted from ES cells grown on gelatinized plates in ES cell growth media containing 100 U/ml LIF using TriReagent according to manufacturer's procedures (Sigma). 50 microg of total protein was resolved by 15% SDS PAGE and transferred to PVDF (Biorad) using 12.5 mM Tris, 96 mM glycine pH 8.3, 20% methanol transfer solution for 1 hour at 200 mA and 25 V limits. Blots were probed with rabbit polyclonal antibodies to H4 ac-K5, H4 ac-K8, H4 ac-K12 (Serotech), H4 3me-K20, H4 acK16, H3 3me-K9, H3 3me-K27 (Upstate), g-H2AX, H3 3me-K4, H3 ac-K14, H3 ac-K18 (abcam) at 1:2000 dilutions overnight at 4degreesC then anti rabbit HRP (Amersham) at 1:4000 dilution for 1 hrs at RT in PBS with 5% NFDM and 0.1% tween 20 through out. Detection was preformed using Pico signal ECL according to manufacturer's procedures (Pierce).
###end p 102
###begin title 103
Tissue Culture Procedures and Luciferase Assays
###end title 103
###begin p 104
###xml 303 307 299 303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tessarollo1">[66]</xref>
ES cells were maintained on mitomycin C treated MEFs in ESC Growth Media (15% FCS (ES Cell grade, Invitrogen), DMEM, essential amino acids, 10 microM mercapto-ethanol, 2 mM glutamine, 100 U/ml LIF (Chemicon International), penicillin and streptomycin). Culture techniques used were described previously [66]. Lines were passaged 3 times onto gelatinized plates to remove MEFs prior to experiments.
###end p 104
###begin p 105
###xml 125 126 125 126 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>
Growth rates of ES cell lines were obtained on gelatinized plates in the absence of feeder layers. Cells were plated @ 1.0x105 in 6 well plates. Cell number was determined every day for 4 consecutive days with changes in ESC Growth media occurring every day.
###end p 105
###begin p 106
Activin-A stimulation of ES cells was performed as follows. ES cell lines were started on gelatinized plates in ESC Growth Media. Cultures were then grown for 2 days in ESC Growth Media without LIF. On the third day, cells were cultured in low serum ESC Growth Media without LIF (same as ESC Growth Media except 0.1% FCS is used instead of 15% FCS) in the presence or absence of 30 ng/ml activin-A (R & D Systems) overnight. Cells were processed using TriReagent according to manufactures standard protocol.
###end p 106
###begin p 107
###xml 312 313 312 313 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 441 442 441 442 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
p300, CBP siRNA knockdowns were preformed as follows. ES cells were grown in ES Cell Growth Medium with 100 U/ml LIF on gelatinized plates. Cells were collected using trypsin and transfected using an Amaxa Nucleofector device using solution ES Cell and program A-30 according to manufacturer's procedures. 2.0x106 ES cells were transfected with 400 nmoles siRNA duplex (Darmacon) or a GFP-Max nucleofection control. Post nucleofection 1.0x106 cells were plated to each well of a 6 well gelatinized tissue culture plate. Cells were stimulated with or without Activin-A in low serum ES Cell growth media as described above. Cells at specified time points were lysed using TriReagent reagent (Sigma) and RNA and protein were purified according to manufacturer's procedures.
###end p 107
###begin p 108
###xml 281 282 281 282 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 407 408 407 408 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 102 107 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
MCF10CA1h cells were grown in a 1:1 mixture of DMEM and Ham's F12 medium (Gibco) supplemented with 5% horse serum. Cells were collected using trypsin and transfected using an Amaxa Nucleofector device using solution V and program T-27 according to manufacturer's procedures. 2.0x106 cells were transfected with 400 nmoles siRNA duplex (Darmacon) or a GFP-Max nucleofection control. Post nucleofection 1.0x106 cells were plated to each well of a 6 well tissue culture plate. Cells were grown for 2 days in growth media and then serum deprived in 1% FBS, DMEM, nonessential amino acids, 10 microM beta-mercaptoethanol overnight. Following serum shock cells were incubated with or without 5 ng/ml TGF-beta1 (R&D Systems) for 1 hour. Cells were lysed using TriReagent reagent (Sigma) and RNA and protein were purified according to manufacturer's procedures.
###end p 108
###begin p 109
###xml 280 281 280 281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 410 411 410 411 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>
P19 cells were obtained from the ATCC (ATCC Number CRL-1825). Cells were grown in 10% FBS, DMEM, 2 mM glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin. Cells were transfected using an Amaxa Nucleofector device using solution V and program C-20 according to manufacturer's procedures. 2.0x106 P19 cells were transfected with 400 nmoles siRNA duplex (Darmacon) or a GFP-Max nucleofection control. Post nucleofection 3.0x105 cells were plated to 12 well plates. Cells were allowed to grow for two days then were serum starved for 18 hours in 0.1% FBS, DMEM, 2 mM glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin. Cells were induced with 5 ng/ml TGF-beta1 (R&D Systems) in low serum growth medium overnight. Cells were lysed using TriReagent reagent (Sigma) and RNA and protein were purified according to manufacturer's procedures.
###end p 109
###begin p 110
Luciferase assays were performed in 12 well format by transfecting 0.6 microg pGL3ti-(SBE)4 or pAR3-Luc, 0.012 microg pCH110 with or without 0.6 microg TbetaRI or 0.6 microg Smad 2-HA and 0.006 microg Smad4-HA, 40.0 pmoles siRNA duplex per well using Lipofectamine 2000 (Invitrogen). In experiments using TGF-beta1 (R&D Systems) or Activin-A (R&D Systems) cells were allowed to grow for 48 hours in 10% FBS, DMEM, 2 mM glutamine prior to adding TGF-beta1 at 5 ng/ml or Activin-A at 30 ng/ml. Cells were induced for 24 hours then lysed with 250 microl siGlow Lysis Buffer (Promega) according to manufacturer's procedures. Transfections utilizing the constitutively active receptors were incubated for 48 hours prior to lysis as above. 50 microl or 100 microl of lysate was assayed with 100 microl Bright-Glow Luciferase Assay Reagent (Promega). Transfection efficiency was normalized to beta-galactosidase levels by assaying 10 microl lysate to 100 microl Beta-Glo Assay Reagent (Promega). Relative Luciferase units were obtained by dividing the luciferase activity levels by the beta-galactosidase levels. Experiments were repeated at least twice and yielded essentially the same results.
###end p 110
###begin p 111
We used P19 cells to test specificity of TGFbeta induction of Bptf protein levels. P19 cells were grown in 10% FBS, DMEM, 2 mM glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin. Ligands were added at the following concentrations; TGFbeta1 (R&D Systems) at 5 ng/ml, FGF4 (R&D Systems) and heparin at 25 ng/ml and 1 ug/ml respectively, BMP4 (R&D Systems) at 10 ng/ml and Wnt3a or L cell control conditioned medium at 1:1 with 10% FBS, DMEM, 2 mM glutamine, penicillin and streptomycin. Cells were incubated overnight and harvested for protein with TriReagent reagent (Sigma) according to manufacturers procedures. Bptf Western blotting was performed as described above.
###end p 111
###begin p 112
Embryoid bodies were cultured as follows. ES cells were treated with trypsin briefly to retain cells in medium sized clumps. Cells were then centrifuged at low speed and resuspended in ESC Growth Medium without LIF and cultured in bacteriological grade petri dishes. ESC Growth Medium without LIF was changed every day for 9 days with minimal disturbance to the embryoid bodies. Samples were taken at specified time points using TriReagent according to manufactures standard protocol or fixed in 10% NBF for histology.
###end p 112
###begin p 113
###xml 12 16 12 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 93 97 93 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>
###xml 301 303 297 299 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sup>
###xml 158 161 <span type="species:ncbi:12305?0.03296277145811789|species:ncbi:36410?3.8779731127197516E-4">CMV</span>
Knockout of Bptf in MEFs was accomplished by infecting litter mate wild type and conditional Bptf (-/Floxed genotype) MEF lines with an adenovirus expressing CMV-Cre. Infection was performed in 6 well plates at sub-confluence (2x105 cells) with 1 ml growth media containing 45 microl Adenovirus @ 1x1010 PFU/ml. Cells were grown for two days in the presence of virus. Following infection cells were divided into 5 wells of a 6 well plate. Cell numbers were recorded every 24 hours with changes in media occurring every 48 hours. A sample of cells was removed at day 4 for Western analysis of Bptf protein levels. Experiment was repeated with two wild type and conditional knockout MEF lines from littermate embryos.
###end p 113
###begin title 114
Chromatin Immuno Precipitation (ChIP)
###end title 114
###begin p 115
###xml 303 307 299 303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Tessarollo1">[66]</xref>
ES cells were maintained on mitomycin C treated MEFs in ESC Growth Media (15% FCS (ES Cell grade, Invitrogen), DMEM, essential amino acids, 10 microM mercapto-ethanol, 2 mM glutamine, 100 U/ml LIF (Chemicon International), penicillin and streptomycin). Culture techniques used were described previously [66]. Lines were passaged 3 times onto gelatinized plates to remove MEFs prior to experiments.
###end p 115
###begin p 116
Activin-A stimulation of ES cells was performed as follows. ES cell lines were started on gelatinized plates in ESC Growth Media. Cultures were then grown for 2 days in ESC Growth Media without LIF. On the third day, cells were cultured in low serum ESC Growth Media without LIF (same as ESC Growth Media except 0.1% FCS is used instead of 15% FCS) in the presence or absence of 30 ng/ml activin-A (R & D Systems) overnight. Following activin-A induction cells were washed with PBS and fixed in 2 mM EGS (Pierce) in 25% DMSO/75% PBS for 30 min followed by 1% PFA in PBS for 30 min. For histone ChIP, cells were fixed in 1% PFA in PBS for 15 min. Following fixation cells were washed 3X in PBS and removed from the tissue culture dish with a cell scraper. Cell pellets were then frozen at -80degreesC. The following day the pellets were thawed and processed using the ChIP procedure published by Upstate biologicals. Antibodies used for pulldown were ChIP grade SNF2H/L (Abcam), H3 3me-K4, H3 3me-K27 (Upstate) and pan H3 (Abcam).
###end p 116
###begin p 117
###xml 300 308 284 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 847 852 801 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gapdh</italic>
Quantitation of pulldown was performed by real time PCR using 2x DyNAmo syprogreen qPCR kit (New England Biolabs) according to manufacturers procedures. Briefly, reactions were composed of 5 microl 1.2 microM forward and reverse primers, 5 microl diluted cDNA template and 10 microl 2x qPCR mix (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Reactions were heated for 10 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 40 cycles at 20 sec at 94degreesC, 20 sec at 60degreesC, 30 sec at 72degreesC. After each cycle the sample was heated to 78degreesC for 10 sec prior to reading sample fluorescence. Pulldowns were quantified as a percentage of input using a dilution series as a standard curve. Histone modification pulldowns are expressed as enrichment relative to histone H3 occupancy under +activin-A conditions. SNF2H/L pulldowns were first normalized to signal at Gapdh and are expressed as the enrichment during +activin-A relative to -activin-A conditions.
###end p 117
###begin title 118
QPCR
###end title 118
###begin p 119
RT reactions were performed on RNA extracted from ES cells, embryoid bodies or P19 cells using TriReagent according to manufacturer's procedures. 5 microg of total RNA was reverse transcribed with Superscript II using oligo dT priming according to manufactures procedures (Invitrogen). cDNA reactions were diluted 5-10 fold and used in a template for PCR.
###end p 119
###begin p 120
###xml 272 280 256 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
###xml 680 685 620 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gapdh</italic>
###xml 689 699 629 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-actin</italic>
Real time PCR was performed using 2x DyNAmo syprogreen qPCR kit (New England Biolabs) according to manufacturers procedures. Briefly, reactions were composed of 5 microl 1.2 microM forward and reverse primers, 5 microl diluted cDNA template and 10 microl 2x qPCR mix (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Reactions were heated for 10 min at 94degreesC, then cycled for 35 cycles at 20 sec at 94degreesC, 20 sec at 60degreesC or 52degreesC, 30 sec at 72degreesC. After each cycle the sample was heated to 78degreesC for 10 sec prior to reading sample fluorescence. Reactions were done in triplicate. DeltaDeltaCt method was used to quantify the relative levels of expression to the Gapdh or beta-actin house keeping genes. Expression levels were then normalized to un-induced cells control cells.
###end p 120
###begin p 121
###xml 202 210 186 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s028">Table S3</xref>
QPCR was performed on E7.5 embryo cDNA as follows. Briefly, reactions were composed of 5 microl 1.2 microM forward and reverse primer pair, 5 microl diluted cDNA template and 10 microl 2x qPCR mix (see Table S3 for primer sequences). Reactions were heated for 10 min at 94degreesC, then cycled at 20 sec at 94degreesC, 20 sec at 60degreesC, and 30 sec at 72degreesC. The number of cycles to maintain linearity was determined using the real time analysis software. PCR reactions within the linear range were resolved using native PAGE.
###end p 121
###begin title 122
Microarray
###end title 122
###begin p 123
###xml 498 499 498 499 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1053 1057 1053 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Carter1">[68]</xref>
###xml 699 704 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 952 957 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 1101 1106 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
For microarray experiments we used one wildtype and two independent Bptf mutant cell lines in 3 culture conditions (LIF+, LIF-, and RA+). Experiments were carried out with 3 biological replications. At the day 3, Triazole (1 ml/well; Invitrogen, USA) was added to the well and total RNAs were extracted using Phase lock gel columns (Eppendorf/Brinkman) according to the manufacturer's protocol. Total RNAs were precipitated with isopropanol, washed with 70% ethanol, and dissolved in DEPC-treated H2O. 2.5 g of total RNA samples were labeled with Cy3-CTP using a Low RNA Input Fluorescent Linear Amplification Kit (Agilent, USA). A reference target (Cy5-CTP-labeled) was prepared from the Universal Mouse Reference RNA (Stratagene, USA). Labeled targets were purified using an RNeasy Mini Kit (Qiagen, USA) according to the Agilent's protocol, quantified by a NanoDrop scanning spectrophotometer (NanoDrop Technologies, USA), and hybridized to the NIA Mouse 44K Microarray v2.2 (whole genome 60-mer oligo; manufactured by Agilent Technologies, #014117) [68]. Transcript copy number estimation using a mouse whole-genome oligonucleotide microarray according to the Agilent protocol (G4140-90030; Agilent 60-mer oligo microarray processing protocol - SSC Wash, v1.0). All hybridizations were carried out in the two color protocol by combining one Cy3-CTP-labeled experimental target and Cy5-CTP-labeled reference target. Microarrays were scanned on an Agilent DNA Microarray Scanner, using standard settings, including automatic PMT adjustment.
###end p 123
###begin p 124
###xml 489 493 489 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Sharov1">[69]</xref>
Differential gene expressions in various cell lines in the standard culture condition were analyzed using the NIA Array Analysis software () which implements ANOVA statistics with two additional methods to reduce the number of false positives: (1) small error variances were replaced with the average error variance estimated from 500 genes with similar signal intensity, and (2) false discovery rates (FDR<0.05) were used to select genes with differential expression, instead of p-values [69]. The FDR method accounts for the effect of multiple hypotheses testing.
###end p 124
###begin p 125
###xml 125 129 125 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Sharov2">[70]</xref>
###xml 82 87 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Gene Ontology analysis and clustering was accomplished using DAVID () and the NIA Mouse Gene Index () using default settings [70].
###end p 125
###begin title 126
GST Pulldowns
###end title 126
###begin p 127
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 128 129 124 125 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 235 240 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
In vitro GST pulldown assays were performed in 50 microl volumes in binding buffer (25 mM Hepes pH 7.4, 100 mM NaCl, 0.5 mM MgCl2, 0.01% NP40), approximately10 microg GST protein fusion bound to a glutathione Sepharose support, 100 ng human NURF complex. Proteins were allowed to bind for 1 hour at 4degreesC with occasional mixing. The beads were washed with 500 microl binding buffer three times at 4degreesC and re-suspended in a final volume of 30 microl.
###end p 127
###begin p 128
###xml 155 159 155 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000241-Ausubel1">[71]</xref>
###xml 225 226 225 226 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
NURF and CBP pulldowns from ES Cell extracts were preformed essentially as described above from 500 mM KCl nuclei extractions made as previously described [71]. The extract was diluted 1:3 with 25 mM Hepes pH 7.4, 0.5 mM MgCl2, 0.01% NP40 with protease inhibitors (Roche) prior to binding to resin bound GST-Smads. The beads were washed with 500 microl binding buffer three times at 4degreesC and re-suspended in a final volume of 30 microl. Proteins were eluted from the beads by adding 5 microl 6x SDS sample buffer and incubating at 37degreesC for 30 min. Proteins were resolved on 4% or 8% polyacrylamide gels and transferred to PVDF (Biorad) and prepared for Western blotting as described above.
###end p 128
###begin title 129
Supporting Information
###end title 129
###begin p 130
Bptf is the homolog of NURF 301.
###end p 130
###begin p 131
###xml 371 375 371 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1064 1068 1052 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 4 9 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 39 49 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 261 271 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
(A) Mouse Bptf is highly homologous to Drosophila NURF301. Major functional domains are conserved between mammals and flies, including nucleosome and transcription factor binding sites, strongly suggesting that Bptf is the homolog of the largest subunit of the Drosophila NURF complex, NURF301. (B) Bptf is predominantly nuclear in cultured P19 cells. siRNA targeting of Bptf results in decreased Bptf signal by Western analysis and a reduction of nuclear fluorescence by anti-Bptf immuno fluorescence in P19 cells. (C) Western analysis of adult brain, testis, spleen, and embryonic stem cells reveals two migrating species, Bptf-H and Bptf-L. (D) Western analysis of total protein extracts from adult tissues using the affinity purified anti-Bptf antisera identifies a single band of high molecular weight predominately found in testis, spleen, and brain. In addition to full length Bptf, we identify a single approximately100 kDa protein which reacts with the antibody exclusively in the adult brain. This protein is identical in size to the previously reported Bptf splice variant FAC1 (Bowser R, Giambrone A, Daves P (1995) Dev Neuroscience 17: 20-37.). (E) A similar western analysis of protein extracts from total embryo proteins identifies high Bptf expression throughout development. The approximately100 kDa cross-reacting band was only found in the adult brain loading standard and not during development.
###end p 131

###xml 23 28 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>

(A) Intron-exon map of mouse Bptf showing alternatively spliced exons and the position of the BptfXG023 trapping vector and BptfDeltaExon2 floxed exon. (B) Diagram of Bptf and BptfXG023 alleles showing tandem trapping vector insertion site between exons 15 and 16. Restriction enzyme sites and positions of Southern blotting probes used for the characterization of BptfXG023 are shown as external probe A and internal probe B. Positions of primers used in multiplex PCR genotyping are designated A, B, and C with A and B complementing genomic sequence spanning the trapping vector insertion site and C the trapping vector. (C) A Southern blot using probe A showing diagnostic restriction enzyme sites confirming the insertion of the trapping vector into Bptf. (D) A Southern blot using Bgl II and probe B showing two bands characteristic of multiple integration events by the trapping vector. Upper band contains sequences external and lower band internal to the trapping vector. (E) A Southern blot of genomic DNA digested with Nsi I, resolved by FIGE and blotted with probe B. A single band was identified in heterozygous mice with an approximate size of 30 Kb, suggesting 3 to 4 trapping vector integration events. (F) Results from multiplex PCR analysis of wild type (+/+), heterozygous (+/-), and homozygous (-/-) BptfXG023 E7.5 embryos using primers A, B, and C. The wild type and mutant alleles are identified by a 325 bp and 500 bp product, respectively. (G) Diagram of Bptf, BptfFloxed-Neo, BptfFloxed, and BptfDeltaExon2 alleles showing the configuration of the integrated targeting vector and its Cre and Flp reaction products. Restriction enzyme sites and positions of Southern blotting probes used for the characterization of BptfDeltaExon2 are shown as external probe 29-31 and internal probes 20.2-20.7, exon2 and 25-26. Positions of primers used in multiplex PCR genotyping are designated A, B, C, E, and F. (H) A Southern blot of heterozygous BptfFloxed-Neo, BptfFloxed, and BptfDeltaExon2 alleles using Sca I and probe 25-26 showing diagnostic restriction enzyme sites confirming the insertion of the targeting vector into Bptf and the products of Cre and Flp recombination. (I) A Southern blot of the same mice as in (H) using Eco RI and probe 25-26. (J) A Southern blot of the same mice as in (H) using EcoRI and probe 29-31. (K) A Southern blot of same mice as in (H) using Eco RI and probe 20.2-20.7. (L) A Southern blot of same mice as in (H) using Kpn I and probe 20.2-20.7. (M) Results from multiplex PCR analysis of wild type Bptf and heterozygous BptfFloxed-Neo, BptfFloxed, and BptfDeltaExon2 alleles using primers E, F, and C. The multiplex PCR strategy yields band sizes of Bptf = 375 bp, BptfFloxed  =  475 bp, and BptfDeltaExon2 = 650 bp. (N) Results from multiplex PCR analysis of wild type Bptf and heterozygous BptfFloxed-Neo, BptfFloxed, and BptfDeltaExon2 alleles using primers A, B, and C. The multiplex PCR strategy yields band sizes of Bptf = 250 bp, BptfFloxed-Neo, BptfFloxed  =  325 bp, and BptfDeltaExon2 = 500 bp.

###begin p 138
###xml 34 39 34 39 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 30 39 30 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>

###begin p 139
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 355 359 355 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 444 449 444 449 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 440 449 440 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 513 517 513 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 522 530 522 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 622 627 619 624 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 618 627 615 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 736 740 733 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 751 764 748 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf-&#946;-Geo</italic>
###xml 894 898 888 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 98 103 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 639 643 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) PCR amplification and sequencing of the upstream junction between the trapping vector and the mouse genome confirm the exact position of the trapping vector to be between exon 15 and 16 of Bptf. (B) RT-PCR results from E7.5 embryos show reduced expression of 3'-RNA sequences and severely reduced exon 15-16 splicing, confirming efficient trapping of Bptf by the trapping vector insertion. (C) DNA sequence of a 5'-RACE amplicon of the BptfXG023 allele from testis shows an in-frame fusion between exon 15 of Bptf and beta-Geo from the trapping vector. (D) Northern analysis of RNA from wild type and heterozygous BptfXG023 disruption mice show predominant transcripts in testis, lungs, spleen, and brain using a probe specific for Bptf mRNA. The Bptf-beta-Geo fusion RNA has the same expression patterns as the wild type allele, suggesting that the trapping vector does not interfere with Bptf regulation at the level of transcription.

###xml 592 606 576 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>

###xml 762 771 742 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>

###xml 775 789 755 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 484 488 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) Wild type (+/+), heterozygous (+/-), and homozygous (-/-) BptfDeltaExon2 embryos at E5.5, E6.5, and E7.5 were removed from their decedua and genotyped using a PCR-based method. Identical to the BptfXG023 allele, reduced growth rates are evident in the homozygous BptfDeltaExon2 embryos as early as E5.5. Mutant embryos from both lines maintained the gross morphology of E5.5 embryos at E6.5 and E7.5 with an overall increase in size. (B) Heterozygous BptfXG023 and BptfDeltaExon2 mice were intercrossed, and wild type, BptfDeltaExon2 heterozygous, BptfXG023 heterozygous, and BptfXG023 / BptfDeltaExon2 trans-heterozygous embryos were dissected from their decidua at E6.5, and genotypes were confirmed by PCR. Trans-heterozygous embryos phenocopy homozygous BptfXG023 or BptfDeltaExon2 embryos, suggesting that the two alleles have an equivalent phenotype.

###xml 750 755 750 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Foxa2</italic>
###xml 873 877 873 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bmp4</italic>
###xml 879 884 879 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Erbb2</italic>
###xml 886 892 886 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgfr2,</italic>
###xml 897 902 897 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mash2</italic>
###xml 1018 1022 1018 1022 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Junb</italic>
###xml 1143 1147 1143 1147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1201 1205 1201 1205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lhx1</italic>
###xml 1357 1358 1357 1358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</italic>
###xml 1363 1367 1363 1367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fgf8</italic>
###xml 1532 1536 1532 1536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bmp4</italic>
###xml 1541 1546 1541 1546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mash2</italic>
###xml 1628 1632 1628 1632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vegf</italic>
###xml 1637 1641 1637 1641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Flk1</italic>
###xml 1838 1842 1838 1842 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1859 1863 1859 1863 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
(A,B) Whole mount in situ RNA hybridization analysis of wild type and mutant E6.5 and E7.5 embryos for Cer1, Nodal, Lefty1, Hex1, Otx2, Hesx1, Lhx1, T, Gsc, Fgf8, Foxa2, Cripto, Junb, Mash2, Bmp4, Erbb2, and Fgfr2 expression. An analysis on wild type and Bptf mutant E6.5 embryos for anterior visceral endoderm (AVE) markers Cer1, Lefty1, and Hex1 show that mutants do not develop an AVE. Bptf mutants show comparable but delocalized Nodal and Cripto expression at E6.5, further suggesting a defect in the development of the AVE. Embryos showed reduced expression of the embryonic ectoderm marker Otx2 and Hesx1 in mutants compared to wild type controls, suggesting defects in the embryonic ectoderm. Primitive streak markers Lhx1, T, Gsc, Fgf8, and Foxa2 also show a significant reduction in expression in mutant at E6.5 compared to wild type. The extra-embryonic markers Bmp4, Erbb2, Fgfr2, and Mash2 are not dramatically affected in mutant when compared to wild type embryos at E6.5. The cell cycle regulatory gene Junb was found to be over expressed in mutant relative to wild type controls at E6.5. Analysis of E7.5 embryos confirms that Bptf mutants do not establish an anterior-posterior axis. Lhx1 is not significantly expressed at E7.5 in mutant compared to wild type, suggesting that primitive streak does not form. Expression of mesoderm markers T and Fgf8 is diffuse in mutant embryos compared to wild type at E7.5, suggesting that the embryo proper becomes unorganized mesoderm-like tissue. The extra-embryonic markers Bmp4 and Mash2 maintain extra-embryonic expression in E7.5 mutant embryos. Angiogenesis markers Vegf and Flk1 show little expression in the extra embryonic portion of the embryo as compared to wild type controls. However, expression is not associated with an allantois, which is severely underdeveloped in Bptf mutant embryos. Bptf expression is largely confined to the embryonic tissues at E7.5.

###xml 1078 1092 1078 1088 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 196 201 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
(A) Retargeting and subsequent transient Cre expression generated conditional heterozygous (not shown), heterozygous (+/-), conditional homozygous (Floxed-Neo/-), and homozygous (-/-) mutant Bptf mouse ES cell clones. Genotypes were confirmed by Southern analysis using an Eco R1 digest and hybridization with Probe 20.2-20.7. (B) Northern analysis of Bptf-mutant ES cell clones using a probe to the 3'-end of the gene shows reduced Bptf transcript levels. (C) RT-PCR analysis of wild type (+/+) and homozygous mutant (-/-) RNA confirms the complete deletion of exon 2 from Bptf transcripts in homozygous mutant clones. Sequence from Bptf mutant PCR products shows the Bptf transcript contains exon 1-3 and 1-4 out of frame splice events as seen in Figure S4C (data not shown). (D) Western analysis of Bptf wild type, heterozygous, conditional heterozygous, and mutant ES cells. Heterozygosity at Bptf results in reduced Bptf protein levels, raising the possibility of haploinsufficiency phenotypes. Homozygous Bptf ES cells mutants do not show Bptf protein, demonstrating that BptfDeltaExon2 is likely to be a null allele. FAC1 expression was not found in ES cells.

(C) Wild type but not mutant day 9 embryoid bodies develop a prominent layer of endoderm on the exterior surface. ###begin p 199
The entire array dataset from each condition was analyzed for statistically significant ontology clusters using DAVID analysis software. Genes that were repressed in expression cluster to highly similar ontology groups and include those involved in "development", "transcription factor activity", and "morphogenesis". Activated gene clusters are highly dependent on condition and include "antigen processing", "peptidase inhibitors", and "cytoskeletal components".

###xml 630 634 630 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 755 759 755 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1007 1011 1007 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1211 1215 1211 1215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1373 1377 1373 1377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 1520 1524 1520 1524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 547 552 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
(A) Genes whose transcription activates, represses, or is unchanged upon LIF- conditions or the addition of retinoic acid (RA) were analyzed for Bptf dependence. Knockout of Bptf results in predominantly reduced activation (repression of activated genes with Bptf knockout) or reduced repression (activation of repressed genes with Bptf knockout) of dynamically regulated genes. (B) Bptf preferentially regulates promoters with bivalent histone modifications. The methylation state expressed as a percentage of all promoters from undifferentiated mouse ES cells. Data was retrieved from Bernstein et. al. (2006) Cell 125:315-326. Bptf-dependent genes from the microarray dataset were grouped based on the promoter's methylation state. From this analysis, Bptf-dependent genes are predominantly enriched for bivalent histone H3 3me-K27, histone H3 3me-K4 over single modified or unmodified promoters. (C) The magnitude of deregulation was compared between activated and repressed genes for each condition of Bptf dependence. A breakdown of gene classes by condition shows that the transcriptome is repressed under LIF+ and RA growth conditions and activated under LIF-. (D) The modifications on bulk histones in Bptf mutant embryonic stem (ES) cells are consistent with a transcriptionally repressed chromatin state. Bulk histones were prepared from wild type (+/+) and two Bptf mutant (-/-) ES cell lines grown in LIF+ growth media. Total protein extracts were then probed for histone modifications by Western blotting. Bptf knockout ES cells have an increase of the repressive H3 3me-K9 and H3 3me-K27 and a decrease of the activating marks H3 ac-K18 and H4 ac-K5. Interestingly, knockout ES cells have an increase in levels of gamma-H2AX, a mark correlated with DNA damage, and H3 3me-K36, a mark of transcription elongation.

###begin p 231
###xml 47 52 47 52 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 43 52 43 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 185 190 185 190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 181 190 181 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 261 265 261 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 426 431 426 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 422 431 422 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 526 531 526 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 522 531 522 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 818 827 818 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000241.s026">Table S1A</xref>
###xml 992 997 992 997 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 988 997 988 997 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 1084 1094 1084 1090 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 1080 1094 1080 1090 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
###xml 1203 1208 1199 1204 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XG023</sup>
###xml 1199 1208 1195 1204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>XG023</sup></italic>
###xml 1231 1241 1227 1233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Exon2</sup>
###xml 1227 1241 1223 1233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf<sup>&#916;Exon2</sup></italic>
(A) Wild type (+/+) and heterozygous (+/-) BptfXG023 males and females were mated in reciprocal crosses and all progeny were genotyped by Southern blotting or PCR. Homozygous (-/-) BptfXG023 embryos were not viable after E7.5 to E8.5, showing that mutations in Bptf are early embryonic lethal. Curiously, more reabsorptions were observed during the dissections than could be accounted for from the death of the homozygous BptfXG023 embryos. To investigate if the origin of the increased lethality was caused by a parental BptfXG023 heterozygous contribution, we crossed heterozygous to wild type males and females in combinations and examined all embryos from E10.5 to E18.5. From these experiments, we observed an increased number of reabsorptions when the mother was heterozygous compared to the wild type controls (Table S1A, b-d). The embryonic lethality was not biased toward heterozygous embryos, as they were found in the expected 1:1 ratio to wild type. These data suggested that BptfXG023 conferred a maternal effect on embryo survival. (B) As in (A), heterozygous (+/-) BptfDeltaExon2 males and females were intercrossed and all progeny were genotyped by Southern blotting or PCR. As with BptfXG023, homozygous (-/-) BptfDeltaExon2 embryos were not viable after E7.5 to E8.5.
###end p 231

###begin p 235
###xml 14 18 14 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
###xml 240 244 237 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bptf</italic>
Phenotypes of Bptf mutants during blastocyst outgrowth and the establishment of the DVE, AVE, and primitive streak were compared to phenotypes from mutations of Smad2/4, Nodal, Wnt3/beta-catenin, remodelers BRG1/SNF2H, and essential genes. Bptf mutations closely resemble mutations in Smad and Nodal pathways.
